016   Figure 1: The C RADLE framework empowers nascent foundation models to perform complex computer tasks
017
      via the same unified interface humans use, i.e., screenshots as input and keyboard & mouse operations as output.
018                                                                A BSTRACT
019
020             Despite the success in specific scenarios, existing foundation agents still strug-
021             gle to generalize across various virtual scenarios, mainly due to the dramatically
022             different encapsulations of environments with manually designed observation and
023             action spaces. To handle this issue, we propose the General Computer Con-
024             trol (GCC) setting to restrict foundation agents to interact with software through
025             the most unified and standardized interface, i.e., using screenshots as input and
026             keyboard and mouse actions as output. We introduce C RADLE, a modular and
027
                flexible LMM-powered framework, as a preliminary attempt towards GCC. En-
                hanced by six key modules: Information Gathering, Self-Reflection, Task Infer-
028
                ence, Skill Curation, Action Planning, and Memory, C RADLE is able to under-
029
                stand input screenshots and output executable code for low-level keyboard and
030             mouse control after high-level planning, so that C RADLE can interact with any
031             software and complete long-horizon complex tasks without relying on any built-
032             in APIs. Experimental results show that C RADLE exhibits remarkable generaliz-
033             ability and impressive performance across four previously unexplored commercial
034             video games, five software applications, and a comprehensive benchmark, OS-
035             World. To our best knowledge, C RADLE is the first to enable foundation agents
036             to follow the main storyline and complete one-hour-long real missions in the com-
037             plex AAA game Red Dead Redemption 2 (RDR2). C RADLE can also create a city
038
                with nearly a thousand people in Cities: Skylines, farm and harvest parsnips in
                Stardew Valley, and trade and bargain with a maximum weekly total profit of 87%
039
                in Dealer’s Life 2. C RADLE can not only operate daily software, like Chrome,
040
                Outlook, and Feishu, but also edit images and videos using Meitu and CapCut.
041             With a unified interface to interact with any software, C RADLE greatly extends
042             the reach of foundation agents by enabling the easy conversion of any software,
043             especially complex games, into benchmarks to evaluate agents’ various abilities
044             and facilitate further data collection, thus paving the way for generalist agents.
045             Video demos and code can be found at https://cradle2024acc.github.io/Cradle.
046
047
      1    I NTRODUCTION
048   Artificial General Intelligence (AGI) has long been a north-star goal for the AI community (Mor-
049   ris et al., 2023). The recent success of foundation agents, i.e., agents empowered by large mul-
050   timodal models (LMMs) and advanced tools, in various environments, e.g., web browsing (Zhou
051   et al., 2023; Deng et al., 2023; Gur et al., 2023; Zheng et al., 2024b;a; He et al., 2024), operating
052   mobile applications (Yang et al., 2023b; Wang et al., 2024b) and desktop software (Zhang et al.,
053   2024; Wu et al., 2024), crafting and exploration in Minecraft (Wang et al., 2023b; 2024a; 2023a),
      and some robotics scenarios (Huang et al., 2022; Brohan et al., 2023b; Driess et al., 2023; Brohan

      Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025

      et al., 2023a), have shown promise. However, current foundation agents still struggle to generalize

                                                              Information
      across different scenarios, primarily due to the dramatic differences in the encapsulation of environ-
054   ments with human-designed observation and action space. Therefore, developing foundation agents
055   applicable to various environments remains extremely challenging.
056   Computers, as the most important and universal interface that connects humans and the increasing
057   digital world, provide countless rich software, including applications and realistic video games for
058   agents to interact with, while avoiding the challenges of robots in reality, such as hardware require-
059   ments, constraints of practicability, and possible catastrophic failures (Raad et al., 2024). Mastering
060   these virtual environments is a promising path for foundation agents to achieve generalizability.
061   Therefore, we propose the General Computer Control (GCC) setting 1 :
062     Building foundation agents that can master ANY computer task via the universal human-style
063     interface by receiving input from screens and audio and outputting keyboard and mouse actions.
064
065   There are many challenges to achieving GCC: i) good alignment across multi-modalities for better
066
      understanding and decision-making; ii) precise control of keyboard and mouse to interact with the
      computer, which has a large hybrid action space, including not only which key to press and where the
067
      mouse to move, but also the duration of the press and the speed of the mouse movement; iii) long-
068
      horizontal reasoning due to the partial observability of complex GCC tasks, which also leads to the
069   demand for long-term memory to maintain past useful experiences; and iv) efficient exploration in
070   a structured manner to discover better strategies and solutions autonomously, i.e., self-improving,
071   which can allow agents to generalize across the various tasks in the digital world.
072
      As shown in Figure 1, we introduce C RADLE, a novel modular LMM-powered framework that
073
      empowers foundation agents towards GCC. C RADLE consists of six key modules: 1) information
074
      gathering, to extract the relevant information from multimodal observations; 2) self-reflection, to
075   rethink past experiences about whether the actions and tasks are successfully completed and reasons
076   for possible failures; 3) task inference, to determine whether to continue current tasks or propose a
077   new task given the current situation; 4) skill curation, to generate, update, and retrieve useful skills
078   for the current task; 5) action planning, to generate specific executable operations for keyboard and
079   mouse control via skills; and 6) memory, for storage, summary, and retrieval of past experiences.
080
      As illustrated in Figure 2, tasks in GCC can be broadly divided into two categories: video game
081   playing and software application manipulation. Video games offer the most challenging tasks in
082   GCC due to several key factors. First, the complexity of game environments requires sophisticated
083   problem-solving and adaptive strategies. Second, long-term reasoning is essential to navigate and
084   succeed in these intricate virtual worlds. Third, understanding and mastering new, complex mechan-
085   ics within games demand rapid learning and cognitive flexibility. Finally, video games test a player’s
086   ability to react quickly and perform precise control and operations, which together create a unique
087   and demanding computational challenge. In addition to the typical embodied control, classical UI
088   manipulation, like menu use and inventory management, is also common during gameplay, which is
089
      similar to the other software applications (Raad et al., 2024). Therefore, video games provide rich
      comprehensive and challenging testbeds to evaluate and improve agents’ various abilities.
090
091   In this work, we conduct extensive experiments to demonstrate the generalizability of C RADLE in
092   such complex environments, while also mastering diverse everyday software applications in distinct
093   domains. We managed to prove that commercial software is out-of-box testbeds under our frame-
094   work. The four selected representative games are: epic AAA 3D role-playing game, RDR2, 2D
095
      pixel-art farming simulation game, Stardew Valley, pawn shop simulation game, Dealer’s Life 2,
      and 3D, top-down view, city-building game, Cities: Skylines. The target set of diverse software ap-
096
      plications for evaluation includes: Chrome, Outlook, CapCut, Meitu, and Feishu, as well as one
097
      comprehensive software benchmark, OSWorld (Xie et al., 2024). We provide a brief introduction
098   to these games in Appendix A, and representative designed tasks for measuring the various abilities
099   of the agent comprehensively in both games and software applications in Appendix Figure 9.
100
101
      Experimental results show that C RADLE exhibits remarkable generalization ability and impressive
      performance across the four previously unexplored commercial video games, the five target software
102
      applications, and the comprehensive contemporaneous OSWorld benchmark. To our best knowl-
103
      edge, C RADLE is the first to enable LMM-based agents to follow the main storyline and complete
104   one-hour-long real missions in a complex AAA game, RDR2. C RADLE also manages to create a
105   city with nearly a thousand people in Cities: Skylines, farm and harvest parsnips in Stardew Valley,
106
          1
107         This setting can be seamlessly extended to other digital devices, i.e., mobile phones, game controllers, and
      virtual reality headsets with standard input and output.

118   trade and bargain with a maximal weekly total profit of 87% in Dealer’s Life 2. Besides, C RADLE
119   can not only operate daily software, like Chrome and Outlook, but also edit images and videos using
120   Meitu and CapCut, and perform office tasks in Feishu. Able to interact with software in a unified
121   manner, C RADLE greatly extends the reach of AI agents by making it easy to convert any software,
122   especially complex games, into benchmarks to evaluate agents’ various abilities and facilitate further
123   data collection, paving the way for generalism. We hope C RADLE can accelerate the development
124   of more powerful foundation agents, thereby advancing the path towards AGI.
125
      2     R ELATED W ORK
126
127   Agents for Software Applications. While previous LLM-based web agents (Deng et al., 2023;
128   Zhou et al., 2023; Gur et al., 2023; Zheng et al., 2024b) show some promising results in effectively
129   interacting with content on webpages, they usually use raw HTML code and DOM tree as input and
130   interact with the available element IDs, ignoring the rich visual patterns with key information, like
131   icons, images, and spatial relations. Multimodal web agents (Hong et al., 2023; Furuta et al., 2023;
132   Yan et al., 2023; He et al., 2024; Zheng et al., 2024a) and mobile app agents (Yang et al., 2023b;
133
      Wang et al., 2024b) have also been explored. Though using screenshots as input, they still need
      to use built-in APIs to get the available interactive element IDs to execute corresponding actions.
134
      Several recent works (Cheng et al., 2024; Zhang et al., 2024; Wu et al., 2024; Kapoor et al., 2024)
135
      aim to apply web agents to more applications by using keyboard and mouse for control. However,
136   they primarily focus on the static websites and lack the generalizability to other domains.
137
138   Agents for Video Games. Several attempts try to develop foundation agents for complex video
139
      games, such as Minecraft (Wang et al., 2023b;a; 2024a), Starcraft II (Ma et al., 2023) and
      Civilization-like game (Qi et al., 2024) with textual observations obtained from internal APIs and
140
      pre-defined semantic actions. Although JARVIS-1 (Wang et al., 2023a) claims to interact with the
141
      environment in a human-like manner with the screenshots as input and mouse and keyboard for
142   control, its action space is predefined as a hybrid space composed of keyboard, mouse, and API.
143   The game-specific observation and action spaces prohibit the generalization of them to other novel
144   games. SIMA(Raad et al., 2024) trained embodied agents to complete 10-second-long basic tasks
145   over ten 3D video games, and the results are promising to be scaled up.
146
      Due to the space limitation, we provide a detailed discussion of the related work in Appendix B.
147
148   3     T HE C RADLE F RAMEWORK
149
150   To pursue GCC, we propose C RADLE, illustrated in Figure 3, a modular and flexible LMM-powered
151   framework that can properly handle the challenges GCC presents. The framework should have the
152   ability to understand and interpret computer screens and dynamic changes between consecutive
153
      frames from arbitrary software and be able to generate reasonable computer control actions for
      precise execution. This suggests that a multimodal model with powerful vision and reasoning capa-
154
      bilities, in addition to rich knowledge of computer UI and control, is a requirement. In this work,
155
      we leverage GPT-4o (OpenAI, 2024b) as the framework’s backbone model.
156
157   3.1   E NVIRONMENT IO
158   Observation and Action Space. C RADLE only takes a video clip, recording the execution of
159   the last action, as input and outputs keyboard and mouse operations to interact with environments.
160   The observation space is made up of complete screen videos with different lengths. For the action
161   space, it includes all possible keyboard and mouse operations, including key_press, key_hold,
      key_release, mouse_move, and wheel_scroll, where keys include both keyboard keys

174
      Figure 3: An overview of the C RADLE framework. C RADLE takes video from the computer screen as input
175   and outputs computer keyboard and mouse control determined through inner reasoning.
176
177
      and mouse buttons. These operations can be combined in various ways to form combos and short-
      cuts, execute rapid key sequences, or coordinate timings. We choose to use Python code to simulate
178
      these operations and encapsulate them into an io_env class.
179
180   Information Gathering. Provided with a video clip as input, it is critical for C RADLE to capture
181   and extract all useful visual and textual information to understand the recent situation and perform
182   further reasoning. Visual information includes layout, imagery, animations, and UI elements which
183
      pose high spatial perception and visual understanding requirements for LMM models. Moreover, we
      depend on their OCR capabilities to extract textual information in images, which usually includes
184
      content (headings and paragraphs), navigation labels (menus and links), notifications, and instruc-
185
      tions to convey messages and guide users. For each environment, we enhance LMMs’ abilities with
186   different tools such as template matching (Brunelli, 2009), Grounding DINO (Liu et al., 2023), and
187   SAM (Kirillov et al., 2023) to provide additional grounding for object detection and localization.
188
189
      Skill and Action Generation As shown in Figure 4, to bridge the gap between semantic actions
      generated by LMMs and OS-level executable actions, C RADLE uses LMMs to generate code func-
190
      tions as semantic-level skills, which encapsulate lower-level keyboard and mouse control. Similar
191
      to how humans improve while playing, these skills can be developed from scratch according to in-
192   game tutorials and guidance, game manuals and settings, or through self-exploration as the game
193   progresses. These skills can also be pre-defined or composited to solve more complex tasks. An ac-
194   tion usually consists of a single or multiple skills instantiated with any necessary parametric aspects,
195   such as duration, position, and speed. An Executor will be triggered to map these semantic actions
196   to the OS-level keyboard and mouse commands to interact with the environment.
197
      3.2   M EMORY
198
199   C RADLE stores and maintains all the useful information from the environment or outputted by each
200   module through a memory mechanism, consisting of episodic memory and procedural memory.
201   Episodic Memory. Episodic memory is used to maintain current and past experiences, including key
202   screenshots from each video observation, and everything useful outputted by LMMs and advanced
203   tools, e.g., textual and visual information, actions, tasks, and reasoning from each module. To
204   facilitate retrieval and storage, periodical summarization is conducted to abstract recently added
205

233
234
235
236
237
238   Figure 5: Illustrative examples of C RADLE’s complete workflow in RDR2 (left), Stardew Valley (middle) and
239   Cities: Skylines (right). Prompts are shown partially for brevity.
240
      multimodal information into long-term summaries. The incorporation of episodic memory enables
241   C RADLE to effectively retain crucial information over extended periods.
242
243   Procedural Memory. This memory is specific to storing and retrieving skills in code form, which
244
      can be learned from scratch as shown in Figure 4, or pre-defined in procedural memory. Skills
      can be added, updated, or composed to the procedural memory in the skill curation module. Same
245
      as Voyager (Wang et al., 2024a), skills are retrieved according to the similarities between their
246
      corresponding embedding and task description.
247
248   3.3   R EASONING
249
      Based on the extracted information from observations and memory, C RADLE conducts high-level
250
      reasoning and then makes the next decision. This process is analogous to “reflect on the past, sum-
251   marize the present, and plan for the future”, which is broken down into the following modules.
252
253   Self-Reflection. The reflection module initially evaluates whether the last executed action was suc-
254
      cessfully carried out and whether the task was completed. Sequential key screenshots from the last
      video observation, along with the previous context for action planning and task inference are fed
255
      to the LMM for reasoning. Additionally, we also request the LMM to provide an analysis of any
256
      failure. This valuable information enables C RADLE to remedy inappropriate decisions or less-than-
257   ideal actions. Furthermore, reflection can also be leveraged to inform re-planning of the task and
258   bring the agent closer to target task completion, better understand the factors that led to previous
259   successes, or suggest how to update or improve specific skills.
260
      Task Inference. After reflecting on the outcome of the last executed action, C RADLE needs to
261
      analyze the current situation to infer the most suitable task for the current moment. We let LMMs
262
      determine the highest priority task to perform and when to stop an ongoing task and start a new one.
263
264   Skill Curation. As the task is specified, C RADLE needs to prepare the tactics to accomplish it,
265   by retrieving useful skills from the procedural memory, updating existing skills, or generating new
266
      ones. The new skill will be stored in the procedural memory for future utilization.
267   Action Planning. C RADLE needs to select the appropriate skills from the curated skill set and
268   instantiate these skills into a sequence of executable actions by specifying any necessary parametric
269   aspects (e.g., duration, position, and target) according to the current task and history information.
      The generated action is then fed to the Executor for interaction with the environment.

                                                         Information
      In this section, we first introduce the practical implementation of the current Cradle framework and
270   then present the empirical results of deploying C RADLE across various challenging environments
271   representative of GCC settings, demonstrating its comprehensive capabilities.
272   4.1   G ENERAL I MPLEMENTATIONS
273
274
      Input. C RADLE applies gpt-4o-2024-05-13 as backbone. It only takes a video clip, which records
      the execution progress of the last action, as input. To lower the frequency of interaction with back-
275
      bone models and reduce the strain on the computer, video is recorded at 2 fps, which proves to be
276
      sufficient in most cases for information gathering without missing any important information.
277
278   Skills. C RADLE uses Python code to simulate keyboard and mouse operations, which is encap-
279   sulated by an io_env class to achieve OS-agnostic interface. Skills are generated based on these
280
      basic operations. We use OpenAI’s text-embedding-ada-002 model (OpenAI, 2022) to generate em-
      beddings for each skill, stored in the procedural memory and retrieved according to the similarities.
281
282   Prompts. Prompts used by each module are initialized by the corresponding templates in
283   Markdown-style format. These prompt templates provide a minimal workflow with basic rules for
284   the module to run and use placeholders of each key for input and output. C RADLE automatically re-
285   trieves the corresponding value for each key in the input from the episodic memory and forms valid
286
      requests to query LMMs with the values and templates. After receiving responses from LMMs,
      C RADLE automatically extracts the keys in the output and stores them in the episodic memory.
287
      Users can freely customize their own prompts without writing any code.
288
289   Apply to new environments. Theoretically, C RADLE can be directly deployed to new video games
290   or other software applications with the default prompt templates and empty procedural memory. Due
291   to the limited ability of current LMMs and the complexity of challenging environments and tasks,
292
      prompt engineering may need to be applied to every module to enhance LMMs’ reasoning ability
      and introduce domain knowledge. Additional tools can also be applied to provide extra grounding
293
      and domain knowledge as part of the prompt input. Procedural memory can be initialized with hand-
294
      craft skills to mitigate the incomplete tutorials provided by the software and the complexity of tasks.
295   Users may need to analyze the task-specific issue and choose a suitable solution. We provide all the
296   implementation details and prompts we use for each software in Appendices D to K.
297
298
      Experimental Settings. If not specifically mentioned, all experiments are conducted in five runs
      under a maximum step limit. For each video game, we hired five human players, who never played
299
      the corresponding game before, to do the evaluation. Before they start the experiments, they will
300
      read the prompts used by Cradle agents for fair comparison. Every player played the task once.
301   We apply human evaluation to all tasks, except for OSWorld, which provides automatic evaluation
302   scripts. Estimated experimental cost of the time and API usage is provided in Appendix C.
303
304
      Task Introduction. As shown in Figure 6 and 7, for RDR2, we mainly focus on evaluating agents
      on the first two complete missions of the main storyline in Chapter I, which can be divided into 13
305
      tasks according to the in-game checkpoints, including but not limited to navigation, NPC interaction,
306
      inventory management, house exploration, and combat. It usually takes a human player about an
307   hour to complete these missions. Few previous studies tackle such long-duration tasks and rich
308   semantic environments. It is an ideal scenario to emulate a novice player learning to play the game
309   from scratch according to the rich in-game tutorials and hints. For Stardew Valley, we propose
310   three essential tasks at the stage of the game, i.e., Farm Clearup: Clear the obstacles on the farm,
311   such as weeds, stones, and trees, as much as possible to prepare for farming; 2) Cultivation: Plant
312   the parsnip seed, water every day and harvest at least one mutual parsnip; 3) Shopping: Go to the
313   general store in the town, which is out of the scope of the current map, to buy more seeds and return
314   home. For Dealer’s Life, the agent is tasked with managing a pawn shop for a week, appraising item
315
      values and haggling with the customers to secure deals. For Cities: Skylines, the task is to build a
      reasonable city ending in as much population as possible, with the initial starting funds of ₡70,000,
316
      and basic road, water and electricity facilities. Moreover, we define five representative domain-
317
      specific tasks for each of the five Software Applications in our diverse target set. We provide an
318   overview of all the tasks for both games and software applications in Appendix Figure 9.
319
320   4.2   P ERFORMANCE ACROSS E NVIRONMENTS
321   Red Dead Red Redemption 2. Figure 6 shows that C RADLE can efficiently complete simple
322   navigation tasks with a few steps like following an NPC or going to specific locations on the ground
323   (e.g., Follow Dutch, Go to Town and Go to Barn). Another following task, Follow Javier, and
      the searching task, Search John, are dangerous for the rugged and winding path up to the snow

340   The second row shows the cumulative steps C RADLE takes to complete each task in the two missions, starting
341   from the beginning of the game. If a task fails, C RADLE can select the ’retry checkpoint’ option to retry the
      task. Skills generated during the task completion are also illustrated in the figure. We only provide key skills

      for brevity. Error bars represent the standard deviation of steps needed to complete each task separately.
343
344

350
351   Figure 7: The first row sequentially shows farm clearup, cultivation and shopping in Stardwe Valley and hag-
352   gling and deal in Dealer’s Life 2. The second row sequentially shows road construction, water pipe laying,
353   wind turbine building, zoning and the display of the city built by C RADLE in Cities: Skylines.
354   mountain with cliffs. Note that Cradle is able to retry the checkpoint automatically according to the
355   game guidance if the task fails. Therefore, C RADLE takes more steps for retrying the task in these
356   dangerous areas. In addition, Cradle spends about one-fourth of the total steps in the task of Protect
357   Dutch, which is a long-horizontal task with nighttime combat. Many key skills are generated in this
358   task for weapon management and shooting movement. The visibility is poor due to the snow falling
359   in the dark, preventing GPT-4o from accurately recognizing and locating enemies or objects and
360   precisely timing decisions, even equipped with Grounding DINO as an additional detection tool.
361
      More times of retry, combined with the need for frequent interactions during combat and the long
      horizon of the task, lead to this task requiring a large number of steps to complete. The success rate
362
      of the combat has significantly improved during the day with much fewer steps for completion, as
363
      shown by tasks like Keep Wolves away. Additionally, indoor tasks like Search for Supplies are also
364   challenging due to GPT4-o’s limited spatial perception, which finds it difficult to locate target objects
365   and ends up circling aimlessly around the house. Moreover, the room contains numerous interactive
366   items unrelated to the task, resulting in much more steps for the agent to complete the task. Overall,
367   C RADLE requires approximately 8,000 steps to complete both missions, taking around 98 minutes
368   of in-game time, compared to the average of 67 minutes for human players. It is the first time for
369   LMM-powered AI agents to exhibit comparable performance in complex AAA games.
370   Stardew Valley. As shown in Table 1, we surprisingly find that GPT-4o struggles with accurately
371   recognizing and locating objects near the player in this pixel-art game. This leads to difficulties for
372   the agent to interact with objects or people, as it requires the player to stand precisely in front of them
373   in the grid (e.g., when entering doors, using a pickaxe to break stones). It explains the inefficiency
374   in the farming task though the agent manages to clear up most of the obstacles in front of the house
375   within 100 steps and poor performance in the shopping task. On the other hand, relying on episodic
376   summarization and task inference, C RADLE manages to obtain the parsnip by watering the seed for
377   four days and harvesting. Given GPT-4’s limited visual capabilities in this game, there is still room
      for improvement in narrowing the gap between C RADLE and human players.

      Software Applications. Figure 8 shows C RADLE’s performance across tasks on five applications.
      Multiple tasks remain challenging. Even with a well-known GUI, like Chrome and Outlook, GPT-4o
413
      still cannot recognize specific UI items to interact with and also struggles with visual context. For ex-
414
      ample, forgetting to press the Save button in an open dialog, or not distinguishing between a nearby
415   enabled button vs. a distant and disabled one (e.g., when posting on Twitter). The phenomenon is
416   more severe in the UI with non-standard layouts, like CapCut, Meitu, and Feishu. Lacking prior
417   knowledge by GPT-4o leads to the failure of task inference and selecting the correct skills.

433   4.3 BASELINE C OMPARISON
434   Since no existing methods are fully applicable to the GCC setting, we select several representative
435   methods with necessary adaptions to make them applicable to GCC, labeling them as "like" in Table
436   3. Compared to C RADLE, React (Yao et al., 2023)-like method only has gather information, skill
437   curation, action planning and procedural memory module, while Reflextion (Shinn et al., 2023)-like
438   method adds a self-reflection and episodic memory, compared to React-like. To show the neces-
439   sity of multimodal input without access to APIs, we let GPT-4o describe the image and then feed
440   the textual description to Voyager (Wang et al., 2024a)-like as input. Additionally, experiments
441
      with GPT-4o and Claude 3 Opus (Anthropic, 2024) as backbone are conducted. Due to the limita-
      tion of requests per minute, other prompting methods like self-consistency (Wang et al., 2022) and
442
      TOT (Yao et al., 2024) are not considered. Note that methods here refer to the agents initialized by
443
      the corresponding framework with game-specific implementations.

      As shwon in Table 3, all the baseline methods can only complete simple and straightforward tasks
      without complex targets and time delays. Compared to React-like method, Reflextion-like method
457
      has better performance in the task of Follow Micah and still fails to complete more complex tasks,
458
      emphasizing the importance of task inference and procedural memory. Voyager-like method that
459   loses vision suffers to accomplish tasks and are the worst of all comparison methods. C RADLE
460   with GPT-4o always has the best performance across all tasks. C RADLE with GPT-4o has the best
461   performance, while Claude 3 Opus fails frequently due to unreliable OCR ability of the guidance,
462   leading to incorrect skill generation and failures of complex tasks.

      Figure 4 provides the detailed performance of each base-

      line method in the Cultivation task in Stardew Valley.

468   ground, they failed to harvest it because GPT-4o failed to
469   recognize the mature parsnip. Episodic memory can help
470   C RADLE record the days of watering and know when
471   the crop can be harvested. Voyager-like method strug-
472   gles with getting out of the house and returning home due

      to the lack of visual input. Claude 3 Opus also has diffi-
      culties in localizing the position of the character and the

      4.4 A BLATION S TUDY
478
479   Besides comparing with other baseline methods, we provide a complete ablation study by system-
480   atically removing each module of Cradle to show the effectiveness in Table 5. We mainly show the
481   results of 6 consecutive subtasks at the beginning of the main storyline, separated from the tasks of
482
      Follow Micah, Hitch Horse and Protect Dutch in RDR2. Note that the combination of skill curation,
      action planning and procedural memory is the minimal unit of our framework. Without any of them,
483
      the agent cannot generate and execute valid actions successfully. So these modules are not ablated.
484
485   The most significant decline in agent capabilities arises from the absence of the information gather-
      ing module. Without this module, the agent is unable to extract key information in the observation,

      Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025

      which is critical for all other modules to function effectively. The second largest impact comes from

      the lack of the self-reflection module, which is instrumental in correcting mistakes and recognizing
      when the agent is stuck, such as in the subtask of Go to Shed. Third, the task inference module is
486   vital for tasks that require strict adherence to guidance, like Switch Weapon. In these cases, the in-
487   game instructions appear only at the beginning of the task, as seen in Follow Micah and Go to Shed.
488   Lastly, episodic memory becomes increasingly important as tasks grow more complex, requiring
489   more steps to complete, such as in Go to Shed and Combat, which involve far more steps than other
490   subtasks. Overall, each module plays a crucial and distinct role in the Cradle framework. Removing
491   or isolating any of them significantly reduces the agent’s effectiveness, underscoring the importance
492   of their integrated function.

      in RDR2. Every subtask is run 5 times. Each of subtasks are run for at most 500 steps.

501           Combat                   0%                0%                                                                                                           0%           0%          20%
502   5 L IMITATIONS AND F UTURE W ORK
503
      Despite C RADLE’s encouraging performance across games and software, several limitations re-
504   main. i) Due to the limited ability of current LMM models, C RADLE struggles in recognizing out-
505   of-distribution (OOD) icons and completing OOD tasks, such as games with non-realistic styles, i.e.,
506   Stardew Valley. As LMMs evolve, they can further improve C RADLE’s performance. ii) Another
507   general bottleneck for LMM-based agents is the latency caused by the limited inference speed of
508   LMMs, which can also be alleviated as LMMs evolve (e.g., Realtime API (OpenAI, 2024a)). iii)
509   Audio, as an important modality, often plays an important role in games and software; which has
510   not been considered in this work. The future work will be enabling C RADLE to process the audio
511   and graphical input simultaneously. iv) As the preliminary attempt towards GCC, most C RADLE’s
512
      modules need to call LMM explicitly to process the input for best performance, resulting in frequent
      interactions with LMM and potentially high costs and long delays. The six modules represent a
513
      problem-solving mindset; as LMM capabilities improve, some or even all of these modules may be
514
      combined into a single request. Exploring other potential GCC frameworks is also promising. v)
515   In this work, we mainly focus on enabling foundation agents to interact with various software in a
516   unified manner without taking training into consideration. As SIMA (Raad et al., 2024) has already
517   shown promising results in a similar setting with trained agents, we will let C RADLE autonomously
518   explore and improve over environments through RL (Tan et al., 2023) or collect expert demonstra-
519   tions for supervised learning (Raad et al., 2024). vi) Though C RADLE is broadly applicable to any
520   computer task, only a few selected tasks are investigated in this work. We plan to expand its appli-
521   cation to a wider range of targets, delve deeper into complex games, and enhance its adaptability
522   for users. vii) Due to the large scope of the experiments conducted in this work, the number of
523
      runs for each task and human participants are limited. A more comprehensive evaluation can be
      beneficial. C RADLE holds great potential to improve effective general computer task completion
524
      and boost research and deployment of foundation agents. However, there is also a risk of unintended
525
      or unsuitable usage, including developing game cheats, incorrect operations of software with harm-
526   ful failures, or other negative agent behavior. Therefore, additional regulations or safeguards are
527   required for secure and responsible deployments across digital and physical environments.
528
529
      6 C ONCLUSION
530   We introduce GCC, a general and challenging setting to control diverse video games and software
531
      with a unified and standard interface, paving the way towards general foundation agents across all
      digital world tasks. To properly address the challenges GCC presents, we propose a novel frame-
532
      work, C RADLE, which exhibits strong performance in reasoning and performing actions to accom-
533
      plish various missions in a set of complex video games and common software applications. To the
534   best of our knowledge, C RADLE is the first framework that enables foundation agents to succeed in
535   such a diverse set of environments without relying on any built-in APIs. The success of C RADLE
536   greatly extends the reach of foundation agents and demonstrates the feasibility of converting any
537   software, especially complex games, into benchmarks to evaluate agents’ general intelligence and
538   facilitate further data collection for self-improvement. Although C RADLE still faces difficulties in
539   certain tasks, it serves as a pioneering work to develop more powerful LMM-based agents towards
      GCC, combining both further framework enhancements and new advances in LMMs.

918
      A        G AME & TASK I NTRODUCTION
919
920
      The four selected representative games are:
921
922   • Red Dead Redemption 2 (RDR2), an epic AAA 3D role-playing game (RPG) with rich story-
923     lines, realistic scenes, and an immersive open-ended world; where players can complete missions
924     by following the instructions, freely explore the world, interact with non-player characters (NPCs)
925     and engage in a variety of activities such as hunting and fishing, in a first- or third-person perspec-
926
        tive. This game offers great challenges in 3D embodied navigation and interaction.
      • Stardew Valley, a 2D pixel-art farming simulation game where players can restore and expand
927
        a farm through carefully planned activities such as planting crops, mining, fishing, and crafting.
928
        Players can build relationships with the villagers, participate in seasonal events, and uncover the
929     mysteries of the valley. The game encourages strategic planning and time management, as each
930     day brings new opportunities and challenges. Players have to balance their energy and resources
931     to maximize their farm’s productivity and profitability.
932   • Dealer’s Life 2, a simulation game where players manage a pawn shop. They must assess the
933     value of items, haggle with customers, and make strategic decisions to grow their business. The
934     game offers a dynamic market influenced by trends, customer preferences, and random events,
935     requiring players to adapt and refine their negotiation tactics.
936   • Cities: Skylines, a 3D, top-down view, city-building game where players take on the role of
937
        a city mayor, tasked with the development and management of a thriving metropolis, engaging
        in urban planning by controlling zoning, road placement, taxation, public services, and public
938
        transportation in an area. They must balance the needs and desires of the population with the
939
        city’s budget, addressing issues such as traffic congestion, pollution, and citizen satisfaction. The
940     game provides a sandbox environment where creativity and strategic thinking are key to building
941     efficient and aesthetically pleasing urban landscapes. It also requires highly precise mouse control.
942

959   Figure 9: Overview of all game tasks (left) in RDR2, Stardew Valley, Cities: Skylines, and Dealer’s Life 2 and
960   application tasks (right) in Chrome, Outlook, CapCut, Meitu, and Feishu.
961
962   B       E XTENDED R ELATED W ORK
963
964
      B.1         E NVIRONMENTS AND B ENCHMARKS FOR C OMPUTER C ONTROL
965
966   Environments and Benchmarks on Software Applications. Simulated environments on com-
967   puters have been popular benchmarks and testbeds for the research community. Earlier computer
968   control environments primarily focused on web navigation tasks (Shi et al., 2017; Liu et al., 2018;
969   Yao et al., 2022; Deng et al., 2023; Zhou et al., 2023; Koh et al., 2024). Recent benchmarks start
970   to include various common software (Kapoor et al., 2024; Xie et al., 2024), aiming to develop a
971   generalist agent in the digital world. However, none of them takes video games into consideration,
      missing a key component of computer control.


                                                                                                  18
       Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


972
       Environments and Benchmarks on Video Games. On the other side, many research environ-
973    ments are built on top of video games, significantly advancing the study of decision-making, espe-
974    cially, reinforcement learning (RL). Examples include but are not limited to Atari games (Bellemare
975    et al., 2013), Super Mario Bros (Kauten, 2018), Google Research Football (Kurach et al., 2020),
976    Minecraft (Johnson et al., 2016; Guss et al., 2019; Fan et al., 2022), Dota II (Berner et al., 2019),
977    StarCraft II (Vinyals et al., 2019; Samvelyan et al., 2019; Ellis et al., 2023), Quake III (Jaderberg
978    et al., 2019), Gran Turismo (Wurman et al., 2022), Diplomacy (Bakhtin et al., 2022) and Civiliza-
979    tion (Qi et al., 2024). Additionally, many custom-built environments, especially grid world and
980    embodied scenarios, are created from scratch in a game-like manner to facilitate agent development,
981
       such as BabyAI (Chevalier-Boisvert et al., 2019), Melting Pot (Leibo et al., 2021), Overcooked (Car-
       roll et al., 2019; Wu et al., 2021; Xiao et al., 2022), VRKitchen (Gao et al., 2019), VirtualHome (Puig
982
       et al., 2018), iGibson (Shen et al., 2021; Li et al., 2021), ProcTHOR (Deitke et al., 2022), Habi-
983
       tat (Manolis Savva* et al., 2019; Szot et al., 2021; Puig et al., 2023), and Generative agents (Park
984    et al., 2023).
985
986    Each of these environments highly relies on the accessibility of the open-source code or provided
987
       built-in APIs. Significant human efforts are required for implementation and encapsulation, enabling
       agent interaction. Therefore, despite the abundance of software and games available for human use,
988
       only a limited number are accessible to agents, especially for commercial closed-source games and
989
       software applications. Additionally, the lack of consensus on environment standards further com-
990    plicates the interaction, as each environment has specific observation and action spaces, tailored to
991    its unique requirements. This variation exacerbates the challenge of enabling agents to interact with
992    diverse environments and collect data with a consistent level of fine-grained semantics to improve
993    the agent’s capabilities. Few agents can complete tasks across multiple environments so far.
994
       Similar to OpenAI Universe (OpenAI, 2016) and SIMA (Raad et al., 2024), our goal is to explore
995
       a unified way that allows agents to interact for measuring and training agents’ abilities across a
996    wide range of games, websites, and other applications without heavy human efforts needed. This
997    approach aims to prove that diverse software applications and games can serve as out-of-the-box
998    environments for AI development.
999
1000
       B.2   LMM- BASED AGENTS FOR C OMPUTER TASKS
1001
1002
       Agents for Software Manipulation. Agents for software applications are developed to complete
1003   tasks such as web navigation (Zhou et al., 2023; Deng et al., 2023; Mialon et al., 2023) and software
1004   application control (Rawles et al., 2023; Yang et al., 2023b; Kapoor et al., 2024). While previous
1005   LLM-based web agents (Deng et al., 2023; Zhou et al., 2023; Gur et al., 2023; Zheng et al., 2024b)
1006   show some promising results in effectively interacting with content on webpages, they usually use
1007   raw HTML code and DOM tree as input and interact with the available element IDs, ignoring the rich
1008   visual patterns with key information, like icons, images, and spatial relations. Recently, multimodal
1009   web agents (Yan et al., 2023; Gao et al., 2023; He et al., 2024; Zheng et al., 2024a; Niu et al.,
1010   2024; Zhang et al., 2024; Wu et al., 2024) and mobile app agents (Yang et al., 2023b; Wang et al.,
1011
       2024b) have been explored. Though using screenshots as input, they still rely on built-in APIs
       and advanced tools to get internal information, like available interactive element IDs, to execute
1012
       corresponding actions, which greatly limits their applicability. Other train-based agents (Hong et al.,
1013
       2023; Furuta et al., 2023; Cheng et al., 2024) also suffer from generalizing to unseen software and
1014   tasks. Moreover, all of these works primarily focus on static websites and software, which greatly
1015   reduces the need for timeliness and simplifies the setting by ignoring the dynamics between adjacent
1016   screenshots, i.e., animations, and incomplete action space without considering the duration of the
1017   key press and different mouse mode. It results in the failure of deployment to the tasks with rapid
1018   graphics changes, e.g., game playing.
1019
       Agents for Game Playing. Several attempts try to develop foundation agents for complex video
1020   games, such as Minecraft (Wang et al., 2023b;a; 2024a), Starcraft II (Ma et al., 2023) and
1021   Civilization-like game (Qi et al., 2024) with textual observations obtained from internal APIs and
1022   pre-defined semantic actions. Although JARVIS-1 (Wang et al., 2023a) claims to interact with the
1023   environment in a human-like manner with the screenshots as input and mouse and keyboard for
1024   control, its action space is predefined as a hybrid space composed of keyboard, mouse, and API.
1025   The game-specific observation and action spaces prohibit the generalization of them to other novel
       games. Pre-trained with videos with action labels, VPT (Baker et al., 2022) manages to output mouse


                                                         19
       Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


1026
       and keyboard control with raw screenshots as input without any additional information. However,
1027   collecting videos with action labels is time-consuming and costly, which is difficult to generalize
1028   to multiple environments. Another concurrent work, SIMA (Raad et al., 2024) trained embodied
1029   agents to complete 10-second-long tasks over ten 3D video games. Though their results are promis-
1030   ing to scale up, they focus on behavior cloning with gameplay data from human experts, resulting in
1031   a high expense.
1032
       In both targeting complex video games and diverse software applications, C RADLE attempts to
1033   explore a new way to efficiently interact with different complex environments in a unified manner
1034   and facilitate further data collection. In a nutshell, to our best knowledge, there are currently no
1035   agents under the GCC setting, reported to show superior performance and generalization in complex
1036   video games and across computer tasks. In this work, we make a preliminary attempt to explore
1037   and benchmark diverse environments in this setting, applying our framework to diverse challenging
1038   environments under GCC and proposing an approach where any software can be used to benchmark
1039   agentic capabilities in it.
1040

1062
       D     G ENERAL I MPLEMENTATION
1063
1064
       Here we introduce the general implementation details of C RADLE. For specialized implementations
       addressing issues unique to their own environment, please refer to the corresponding section.
1065
1066   Hardware. All software and games can be run on regular Windows 10 machines, except for RDR2,
1067   which is tested on machines with RTX-4090 GPU separately.
1068   Backbone Model. We employ GPT-4o (OpenAI, 2024b), currently one of the most capable LMM
1069   models, as the framework’s backbone model. If not mentioned explicitly, all the experiments are
1070   done with gpt-4o-2024-05-13. Temperature is set to 0 to lower the variance of the text generation.
1071   Same as Voyager (Wang et al., 2024a), we use OpenAI’s text-embedding-ada-002 model (OpenAI,
1072   2022) to generate embeddings for each skill, stored in the procedural memory and retrieved accord-
1073   ing to the similarities.
1074   Evaluation Methods. Unlike conventional research benchmarks, which usually provide grounding
1075   signals for evaluation, it is difficult to have a unified and general method to determine whether a task
1076   is completed automatically in diverse software, especially in video games. Similarly to SIMA (Raad
1077   et al., 2024), we apply human evaluation to all tasks across application software and games. More-
1078   over, to provide more quantitative results and a comparison baseline, we provide results for the
1079   OSWorld (Xie et al., 2024) benchmark, a contemporaneous benchmark that provides evaluation
       scripts for at least one solution per task.


                                                             20
       Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


1080
       Observation Space. C RADLE only takes a video clip, which records the progress of execution of
1081   the last action, as input. To lower the frequency of interaction with backbone models and reduce the
1082   strain on the computer, video is recorded at 2 fps (a screenshot every 0.5 seconds), which proves
1083   to be sufficient in most cases for information gathering without missing any important information.
1084   It is important to note that, due to the dynamism of the RDR2 and Stardew Valley and the LMM
1085   inference and communication latency, we must pause those game environments while waiting for
1086   backbone model responses. Other environments execute continuously.
1087   Action Space. For the action space, it includes all possible keyboard and mouse operations, includ-
1088   ing key_press, key_hold, key_release, mouse_move, mouse_click, mouse_hold,
1089   mouse_release, and wheel_scroll, which can be combined in different ways to form com-
1090   bos and shortcuts, use keys in fast sequence, or coordinate timings. We choose to use Python code
1091   to simulate these operations and encapsulate them into an io_env class. Skill code needs to be
1092   generated by the agent in order to utilize such functions and affordances so executed actions take
1093   effect. Table 7 illustrates C RADLE’s action space.
1094
1095   Table 7: Action space in the C RADLE framework, including action attributes. Coordinate system is either

1122
1123
1124   It is important to note that, while some works (e.g., AssistantGUI (Gao et al., 2023), Omni-
1125   ACT (Kapoor et al., 2024) and OSWorld (Xie et al., 2024)) use PyAutoGUI 3 for keyboard and
1126   mouse control, this approach does not work in all applications, particularly in modern video games
1127   using DirectX 4 . Moreover, such work chooses to expose a subset of the library functionality in its
1128
       action space, ignoring dimensions like press duration and movement speed, which are critical in
       many scenarios (e.g., RDR2, for opening the weapon wheel and changing view).
1129
1130
1131      3
           Python library that provides a cross-platform GUI automation module - https://github.com/
1132   asweigart/pyautogui
         4
1133       Microsoft DirectX graphics provides a set of APIs for high-performance multimedia apps - https://
       learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/directx


                                                         21
       Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


1134
       To ensure wide game and software compatibility and accommodate different operating systems, in
1135   our current implementation we use the similar PyDirectInput library 5 and PyAutoGUI for keyboard
1136   control, utilize AHK 6 and write our own abstraction (using the ctypes library 7 ) to send low-level
1137   mouse commands to the operating system for mouse control. For increased portability and ease of
1138   maintenance, all keyboard and mouse control is encapsulated in a class, called IO_env.
1139
       Notably, our low-level control wrapper is adapted for both MacOS and Windows systems, mak-
1140
       ing the OS transparent to us. At the software window level, we implemented automatic switching
1141   between the target software window and the window running the agent (using Python ctypes for
1142   Windows and AppleScript for MacOS 8 ).
1143
1144
       Procedure Memory. This memory stores pre-defined basic skills and the generated skills captured
       from the Skill Curation. However, as we continuously obtain new skills during game playing, the
1145
       number of skills in procedural memory keeps increasing, and it is hard for GPT-4o to precisely select
1146
       the most suitable skill from the large memory. Thus, similar to Voyager (Wang et al., 2024a), we
1147   use OpenAI’s text-embedding-ada-002 model (OpenAI, 2022) to generate embeddings for each skill
1148   and store pre-defined basic skills and any generated skills captured from Skill Curation, along with
1149   their embeddings in a procedural memory. We retrieve a subset of skills, that are relevant to the
1150   given task, and then let GPT-4o select the most suitable one from the subset. In the skill retrieval,
1151   we pre-compute the embeddings of the documentations (code, comments and descriptions) of skill
1152   functions, which describe the skill functionality, and compute the embedding of the given task.
1153   Then we compute the cosine similarities between the skill documentation embeddings and the task
1154   embedding. The higher similarity means that the skill’s functionality is more relevant to the given
1155
       task. We select the top K skills with the highest similarities as the subset. Using similarity matching
       to select a small candidate set simplifies the process of choosing skills.
1156
1157   Episodic Memory. This memory stores all the useful information provided by the environment and
1158   LMM, which consists of short-term memory and long-term summary.
1159   The short-term memory stores the screenshots within the recent k interactions in game playing and
1160   the corresponding information from other modules, e.g., screenshot descriptions, task guidance,
1161   actions, and reasoning. We set k to five, and it can be regarded as the memory length. Information
1162   stored over k interactions ago will be forgotten from direct short-term memory. Empirically, we
1163   found that recent information is crucial for decision-making, while a too-long memory length would
1164   cause hallucinations. In addition, other modules continuously retrieve recent information from short-
1165   term memory and update the short-term memory by storing the newest information.
1166   For some long-horizon tasks, short-term memory is not enough. This is because the completion of
1167   a long-horizon task might require historical information from a long steps ago. For example, the
1168   agent might do a series of short-horizon tasks during a long-horizon task, which makes the original
1169   long-horizon task forgotten in short-term memory. To maintain the long-term valuable information
1170   while avoiding the long-token burden of GPT-4o, we propose a recurrent information summary as
1171   long-term memory, which is the text summarization of experiences in game playing, including the
1172   ongoing task, the past entities that the player met, and the past behaviors of the player and NPCs.
1173   In more detail, we provide GPT-4o with the summarization before the current screenshot and the
1174   recent screenshots with corresponding descriptions, and GPT-4o will make a new summarization
1175   by organizing the tasks, entities, and behaviors in the time order with sentence number restriction.
1176   Then we update the summarization to be the newly generated one, which includes the information
1177   in the current screenshot. The recurrent summarization update, inspired by RNN, achieves linear-
1178   time inference by preserving a hidden state that encapsulates historical input. This method ensures
1179
          5
1180        Python library encapsulating Microsoft’s DirectInput calls for convenience manipulating keyboard keys -
1181   https://github.com/learncodebygaming/pydirectinput
          6
1182        A fully typed Python wrapper around AutoHotkey to keyboard and mouse control - https://github.
       com/spyoungtech/ahk
1183      7
            Python library that provides C compatible data types, and allows calling functions in DLL/.so binaries -
1184
       https://docs.python.org/3/library/ctypes.html
1185      8
            AppleScript is a scripting language created by Apple, which allows users to directly control scriptable
1186   applications, as well as parts of MacOS - https://developer.apple.com/library/archive/
1187   documentation/AppleScript/Conceptual/AppleScriptLangGuide/introduction/
       ASLR_intro.html


                                                            22
       Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


1188
       the compactness of summarization token lengths and recent input data. Furthermore, the incorpora-
1189   tion of long-term memory enables the agent to effectively retain crucial information over extended
1190   periods, thereby enhancing decision-making capabilities.
1191
1192
       Information Gathering. Given the video clip as input, we mainly depend on GPT-4o’s OCR capa-
       bilities to extract textual information in the keyframes, which usually contain critical guidance and
1193
       notifications for the current situation. We also rely on GPT-4o’s visual understanding to analyze the
1194
       visual information in the frames. Besides, we augment LMMs’ visual understanding via some tools,
1195   like template matching (Brunelli, 2009), Grounding DINO (Liu et al., 2023), and SAM (Kirillov
1196   et al., 2023), to provide additional grounding for object detection and segmentation. Some visual
1197   prompting tricks, like drawing axes and colorful directional bands, are also applied to enhance the
1198   GPT-4o’s visual ability.
1199
       Task Inference. After reflecting on the outcome of the last executed action, We let GPT-4o analyze
1200
       the current situation to infer the most suitable task for the current moment and estimate the highest
1201   priority task to perform and when to stop an ongoing task and start a new one.
1202
1203   Skill Curation. GPT-4o is required to strictly follow the provided interfaces and examples to gen-
1204
       erate the corresponding code for new skills. Moreover, GPT-4o is required to include documenta-
       tion/comments within the generated code, delineating the functionality of each skill. Procedural
1205
       Memory where skills are stored will then check whether the code is valid, whether the format of
1206
       documentation is right, and whether any skill with the same name already exists. If all conditions
1207   are passed, the newly generated skill is persisted for future utilization.
1208
1209   Action Planning. GPT-4o needs to select the appropriate skills from the curated skill set and in-
1210
       stantiate these skills into a sequence of executable actions by specifying any necessary parametric
       aspects (e.g., duration, position, and target) according to the current task and history information.
1211
       The generated action is then fed to the Executor for interaction with the environment.
1212
1213
1214   E     R ED D EAD R EDEMPTION II
1215
1216
       E.1   I NTRODUCTION TO RDR2
1217
1218   Red Dead Redemption II (RDR2) is an epic AAA Western-themed action-adventure game by Rock-
1219   star Games. As one of the most famous and highest-selling games in the world, it is widely ac-
1220   knowledged for its movie-like realistic scenes, rich storylines, and immersive open-ended world.
1221   The game applies a typical role-playing game (RPG) control system, played from a first- or third-
1222   person perspective, which uses WASD for movement, mouse control for view changing, first- or
1223   third-person shooting for combat, and inventory and manipulation.
1224   For most of the game, players need to control the main character, Arthur Morgan, upon choosing
1225   to complete mission scenarios following the main storyline. Otherwise, they can freely explore the
1226   interactive world, such as going hunting, fishing, chatting with non-player characters (NPCs), train-
1227   ing horses, witnessing or partaking in random events, and participating in side quests. As the main
1228   storyline progresses, different skills are gradually unlocked. As a close-source commercial game,
1229   no APIs are available for obtaining additional game-internal information nor pre-defined automation
1230   actions. Following its characteristics, this game serves as a fitting and challenging environment for
1231
       the GCC setting and a comprehensive benchmark for embodiment.
1232
1233   E.2   O BJECTIVES
1234
1235   In Chapter 1 of RDR2, the first two missions of the main storyline are Outlaws from the West
1236   and Enter, Pursued by a Memory. These missions serve as the tutorial content for RDR2, guiding
1237   players step-by-step into the role of Arthur. They immerse the player in the story’s development
1238
       while teaching the game’s controls and mechanics.
1239   We divided Mission 1 and Mission 2 into 8 and 5 tasks respectively based on the checkpoints within
1240   each mission. Each checkpoint may present failure scenarios. For example, in Mission 1, there are
1241   six failure scenarios: i) Assaults, kills, or abandons Dutch or Micah; ii) Allows Dutch or Micah to be
       killed; iii) Abandons the homestead; iv) Assaults, kills, or abandons their horse; v) Assaults, kills,

       Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025

       To evaluate C RADLE’s capabilities in an open-world environment, Mission 3 is designed as a hard
1262
       open-ended task. Unlike the first two tutorial missions, it does not include any checkpoints. Conse-
1263
       quently, the entire Mission 3 is treated as a single, comprehensive task. Although we do not subdi-
1264   vide Mission 3 into finer tasks, we aim to identify key points to facilitate a clearer understanding of
1265   Mission 3 for the reader.

       Tables 8 and 9 provide a brief introduction of each task in the first two missions of the main storyline
       and an open-ended mission, along with approximate estimates of their difficulty. Due to GPT-4o’s
1268
       poor performance in spatial understanding and fine-manipulation skills, it can be challenging for
1269
       our agent to perform certain actions, like entering or leaving a building, or going to precise indoor
1270   locations to retrieve specific items. Additionally, the high latency of GPT-4o’s responses also makes
1271   it harder for an agent to deal with time-sensitive events, e.g., during combat.

1273
       E.3     I MPLEMENTATION D ETAILS
1274
1275   Our experiments are based on the latest version of RDR2, ‘Build 1491.50’. As shown in Figure
1276   14, strictly following the GCC setting, our agent takes the video of the screen as input and outputs
1277   keyboard and mouse operations to interact with the computer and the game. An observation thread
1278   is responsible for the collection of video frames from the screen and each video clip records the
1279   whole in-game process since executing the last action.
1280
       Information Gathering. To extract keyframes from the video observation, we utilize the VideoSub-
1281   Finder tool 9 , a professional subtitle discovery and extraction tool. These keyframes usually contain
1282   rich meaningful textual information in the game, which are highly relevant to the completion of
1283   tasks and missions (such as character status, location, dialogues, in-game prompts and tips, etc.) We
1284   use GPT-4o to extract and categorize all the meaningful contexts in these keyframes and perform
1285   OCR, and call this processing "gathering text information". Then, to save interactions with GPT-4o,
1286   we only let GPT-4o provide a detailed description of the last frame of the video.
1287   While GPT-4o exhibits impressive visual understanding abilities across various CV tasks, we find
1288   that it struggles with spatial reasoning and recognizing some game-specific icons. To address these
1289   limitations, we add a visual augmentation sub-module within our Information Gathering module.
1290   This augmentation step serves two main purposes: i) utilize Grounding DINO (Liu et al., 2023), an
1291   open-set object detector, to output precise bounding boxes of possible targets in an image and serve
1292   as spatial clues for GPT-4o; and ii) perform template matching (Brunelli, 2009) to provide icon
1293   recognition grounding truth for GPT-4o when interpreting instructions or menus shown on screen.
1294   As LMM capabilities mature, it should be possible to disable such augmentation.
1295
          9
              VideoSubFinder standalone tool - https://sourceforge.net/projects/videosubfinder/

       Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025

1336
1337
       Self-Reflection. The reflection module mainly serves to evaluate whether the previously executed
1338   action was successfully carried out and whether the current executing task is finished. To achieve
1339   this, we uniformly sample at most 8 sequential frames from the video observation since the execution
1340   of the last action and use GPT-4o to estimate the success of its execution. Additionally, we expect
1341   GPT-4o can also provide analysis for any failure of the last action (e.g., the move-forward action
1342   failed and the cause could be the agent was blocked by an obstacle). With such valuable information
1343   as input for Action Planning, including the failure/success of the last action and the corresponding
1344   analysis, the agent is capable of attempting to remedy an inappropriate decision or action execution.
1345   Moreover, some actions require prolonged durations, such as holding down specific keys, which can
1346   coexist or interfere with other actions decided by subsequent decisions. Consequently, the reflection
1347   module must also decide whether an ongoing action should continue to be executed. Furthermore,
1348   self-reflection can be leveraged to dissect why the last action failed to bring the agent close to the
1349   target task completion, better understand the factors that led to the successful completion of the
       preceding task, and so on.

1393
1394   Besides, we observe that instead of providing GPT-4o with sequential high-resolution images for
1395   self-reflection, low-resolution images make it easier for GPT-4o to understand the relation among
1396   the sequential screenshots and capture dynamic changes, resulting in a significantly higher success
1397   rate of detecting whether the action is executed successfully and take any effect. We hypothesize that
1398   since a high-resolution image can cost as many as 2000 tokens, too many high-resolution images
1399   make GPT-4o fail to capture the overall changes across screenshots and be caught up in the local
1400
       details.
1401   Task Inference. During gameplay, we let GPT-4o propose the current task to perform whenever it
1402   believes it is time to start a new task. GPT-4o also outputs whether the task is a long- or short-horizon
1403   task when proposing a new task. Long-horizon tasks, such as traveling to a location, typically require
       multiple iterations, whereas short-horizon tasks, like picking up an item or conversing with someone,
